Life of Imam al-Bayjuri

Biography of Ibrahim al-Laqani
Biography of the poet Ibrahim al-Laqani, covering name, lineage, birth, death, and nisbah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the biography of Imam Ibrahim al-Laqani, the author of Jawharat al-Tawhid, including his name, lineage, birth, death, and his nisbah.

Core Idea
Ibrahim al-Laqani, a humble scholar of noble descent, authored Jawharat al-Tawhid.

Before studying the text of Jawharat al-Tawhid, it is valuable to know something about its author, Imam Ibrahim al-Laqani. His biography gives us insight into his scholarly lineage and the context of his work. In this lesson, we will learn about his name, his noble lineage, his birth and death dates, and the meaning of his nisbah 'al-Laqani'.

Guided Path
1
Read the biography passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the key details about the author's life.
Notice the humility mentioned in the lineage.
2
Identify key details
List the author's full name, lineage, birth period, death year, and the meaning of 'al-Laqani'.
The birth year is deduced from his son's birth.
3
Understand the nisbah
Learn that 'al-Laqani' refers to the village Laqanah in Egypt, and note the correct pronunciation without shaddah on the qaf.
This corrects a common mistake.
4
Reflect on author's humility
Notice that al-Laqani concealed his noble lineage out of humility. Consider how this virtue impacted his scholarship.
5
Review the sources
The passage ends with references. Understand that scholars rely on such sources for biographical accuracy.
This builds trust in the presented information.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمة الناظم
العلامة الشَّيخ برهان الدين إبراهيم اللَّقَاني (١) رحمه الله تعالى
،
اسمه ونسبه:
هو الشَّيخ برهان الدين إبراهيم بن إبراهيم بن حسن بن علي بن علي بن علي بن عبد القدوس بن الولي الشهير محمد بن هارون، أبو الإمداد اللقاني المالكي، المصري لقبه برهان الدين وكنيته أبو الإمداد وأبو إسحاق وله اتصال هو وقبيلته المنحدر منها بالنسب الشريف، وكان لا يُظهره تواضعاً منه .
،
وأما عن مولده فلم تُعين كتب التراجم تاريخ مولده، ولكن ولد قبل (٩٦٠هـ)؛ لأن الشيخ عبد السلام ابنه ولد (۹۷۱هـ)، وأرّخ تاريخ وفاته سنة (١٠٤١هـ)
نسبته
اللقاني : : نسبة إلى (لَقَانَة) كـ(سَحابة)، قرية من قرى مصر كما ذكر الزبيدي في «تاج العروس»، قال : وقد وردتها، وقال المحبي في خلاصة الأثر» (٦/١) : هو بفتح اللام ثم قاف وألف ونون ولم يذكر التشديد ، أي : تشديد القاف خطأ.
(1) مصادر الترجمة :
الأعلام للزركلي (۲۸/۱).
- فهرس الفهارس) (۱۳۱).
- خلاصة الأثر» (٦/١-٩).
-
. الخطط التوفيقية لعلي مبارك (١٥).
فهارس الأزهرية» (۲۹۷/۱)
Biography of the poet, the eminent scholar, Shaykh Burhan ad-Din Ibrahim al-Laqani (1) - may Allah have mercy on him.

His name and lineage:
He is the Shaykh Burhan ad-Din Ibrahim ibn Ibrahim ibn Hasan ibn Ali ibn Ali ibn Ali ibn 'Abd al-Quddus ibn the famous saint Muhammad ibn Harun, Abu al-Imdad al-Laqani al-Maliki, the Egyptian. His title is Burhan ad-Din, and his kunyah is Abu al-Imdad and Abu Ishaq. He and his tribe descending from him have connection to the noble lineage, but he did not manifest it out of humility.

As for his birth, the biographical books did not specify his birth date, but he was born before (960 AH) because his son Shaykh 'Abd as-Salam was born in (971 AH). His death date is recorded as the year (1041 AH).

His nisbah (attribution):
Al-Laqani: attributed to (Laqanah) like (Sahabah), a village in Egypt as mentioned by az-Zabidi in 'Taj al-'Arus'. He said: I have visited it. Al-Muhibbi said in 'Khulasat al-Athar' (1/6): It is with a fatha on the lam, then qaf, alif, and nun, and he did not mention tashdid, meaning that tashdid on the qaf is a mistake.
(1) Sources of the biography:
- Al-A'lam by az-Zarkali (1/28).
- Fihris al-Faharis (131).
- Khulasat al-Athar (1/6-9).
- Al-Khitat at-Tawfiqiyya by 'Ali Mubarak (15).
- Faharis al-Azhariyya (1/297).
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage provides a biography of the poet Ibrahim al-Laqani, the author of Jawharat at-Tawhid. It begins with his full name, lineage, and notable titles. His lineage goes back to a famous saint, Muhammad ibn Harun. He is attributed to the Maliki school and is Egyptian. He had multiple kunyahs: Abu al-Imdad and Abu Ishaq. The passage notes that he and his tribe have a connection to noble lineage (likely meaning descent from the Prophet), but he hid it out of humility. His birth date is unknown, but it is deduced that he was born before 960 AH because his son 'Abd as-Salam was born in 971 AH. His death is recorded as 1041 AH. The attribution 'al-Laqani' is explained as coming from the village Laqanah in Egypt, with a note on the correct pronunciation: the lam is fatha, qaf is not doubled. The passage concludes by listing five sources for the biography.

Key Terms
ترجمة
برهان الدين إبراهيم اللقاني
لقاني
نسب
مولد
وفاة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some pronounce 'al-Laqani' with a shaddah (double qaf), thinking it is correct.
Correction: The correct pronunciation is with a single qaf: al-Laqani (without shaddah), as stated in the passage.

Checkpoint
How do we know that Ibrahim al-Laqani was born before 960 AH?
A) His birth date is recorded in biographical works
B) His son was born in 971 AH
C) He died in 1041 AH
D) He was a student of a scholar born in 960 AH

Key Takeaway
Imam Ibrahim al-Laqani, a humble scholar with noble lineage, was born before 960 AH and died in 1041 AH, and his nisbah comes from a village in Egypt.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Imam al-Laqani concealed his noble lineage out of humility. What honor, accomplishment, or blessing in your life do you find hardest to hide? Will you intentionally conceal it today for Allah's sake?
?
The correct pronunciation of 'al-Laqani' is a detail easily overlooked. How meticulously do you respect the names and attributes of scholars? Will you correct yourself the next time you mispronounce a scholar's name?
?
His birth date is unknown, but his death is recorded. You will die on a date known only to Allah. Are you living today as if that date could be tomorrow? What is one change you will make today to prepare for that meeting?

Who Was al-Laqqani? Name, Lineage, and Nisbah
Biographical details of al-Laqqani: his full name, lineage, birth estimate, death, and the meaning of his nisbah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key biographical details of the author al-Laqqani, including his full name, lineage, dates, and the meaning of his nisbah.

Core Idea
The author's nisbah comes from an Egyptian village, not a religious title.

Before studying a text, it is valuable to know its author. This passage introduces us to al-Laqqani: his name, his honorable lineage, his life span, and the origin of his surname. Understanding these details places the Jawharat al-Tawhid in its proper context.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage once
Read the full Arabic passage without analyzing. Focus on the long chain of names. Then read the translation to get the gist.
Notice the repetition of 'Ali' in the lineage.
2
Identify the birth and death information
The passage does not give an exact birth year but infers it from his son's birth. Note the death year 1041 AH.
3
Analyze the nisbah explanation
Understand that 'al-Laqqani' is derived from the village 'Laqana'. The correct pronunciation is with a fatha on the lam and no tashdid on the qaf.
Al-Muhibbi clarifies a common mistake.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هو الشَّيخ برهان الدين إبراهيم بن إبراهيم بن حسن بن علي بن علي بن علي بن عبد القدوس بن الولي الشهير محمد بن هارون، أبو الإمداد اللقاني المالكي، المصري لقبه برهان الدين وكنيته أبو الإمداد وأبو إسحاق وله اتصال هو وقبيلته المنحدر منها بالنسب الشريف، وكان لا يُظهره تواضعاً منه .، وأما عن مولده فلم تُعين كتب التراجم تاريخ مولده، ولكن ولد قبل (٩٦٠هـ)؛ لأن الشيخ عبد السلام ابنه ولد (۹۷۱هـ)، وأرّخ تاريخ وفاته سنة (١٠٤١هـ) ، نسبته: اللقاني : : نسبة إلى (لَقَانَة) كـ(سَحابة)، قرية من قرى مصر كما ذكر الزبيدي في «تاج العروس»، قال : وقد وردتها، وقال المحبي في خلاصة الأثر» (٦/١) : هو بفتح اللام ثم قاف وألف ونون ولم يذكر التشديد ، أي : تشديد القاف خطأ.
He is the Shaykh Burhan al-Din Ibrahim ibn Ibrahim ibn Hasan ibn Ali ibn Ali ibn Ali ibn Abd al-Quddus ibn al-Wali al-Shahir Muhammad ibn Harun, Abu al-Imdad al-Laqqani al-Maliki, al-Misri; his honorific is Burhan al-Din and his kunya is Abu al-Imdad and Abu Ishaq. He and his tribe descending from it have connection to the noble lineage, and he would not display it out of humility. As for his birth, the biographical books did not specify his birth date, but he was born before (960 AH) because his son Shaykh Abd al-Salam was born in 971 AH, and his death date was recorded as (1041 AH). His nisbah: al-Laqqani is a nisbah to (Laqana) like (Sahaba), a village in Egypt as al-Zabidi mentioned in Taj al-Arus, saying: I visited it. And al-Muhibbi said in Khulasat al-Athar (6/1): it is with a fatha on the lam, then qaf, alif, and nun, and he did not mention tashdid, meaning that tashdid of the qaf is a mistake.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage provides biographical data about the author. It begins with his full name and lineage, tracing him back through several generations to a well-known saint, Muhammad ibn Harun. It gives his various kunyas and notes his connection to the noble lineage of the Prophet, which he did not openly claim out of humility. Next it covers his birth and death: the exact birth year is unknown but inferred to be before 960 AH because his son was born in 971 AH; his death was in 1041 AH. Finally it explains his nisbah 'al-Laqqani', tracing it to the village of Laqana in Egypt, citing al-Zabidi and al-Muhibbi on the correct pronunciation (with a fatha on the lam and no tashdid on the qaf).

Key Terms

لَقَانَة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'al-Laqqani' indicates a town with a qaf with tashdid
Correction: The author clarifies it is from 'Laqana' with a single qaf, as confirmed by al-Muhibbi.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct pronunciation of the nisbah 'al-Laqqani'?
A) With a dhamma on the lam and tashdid on the qaf
B) With a fatha on the lam and no tashdid on the qaf
C) With a kasra on the lam and a shadda on the qaf
D) With a fatha on the lam and a shadda on the qaf

Key Takeaway
Al-Laqqani's biography shows his noble lineage and clarifies that his nisbah comes from an Egyptian village pronounced with a fatha and no tashdid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Laqqani concealed his noble lineage out of humility. Is there any part of your background, status, or achievement that you subtly flaunt? What would it cost you to hide it for the sake of Allah?
?
His nisbah comes from an obscure village, not a famous city. Do you seek honor from where you come from or what you have attained? How can you root your identity solely in your relationship with Allah?
?
The source notes that al-Laqqani's birth year is uncertain. Are you comfortable with anonymity and not being remembered? If you were to die and leave no trace except your deeds, would that satisfy you?

Life of Imam al-Bayjuri

The Virtue and Scholarly Status of Imam al-Laqqani
Description of al-Laqqani's vast knowledge, his role as a reference, and his personal qualities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key virtues and scholarly attributes of Imam al-Laqqani as described by his biographer.

Core Idea
Al-Laqqani combined vast scholarship with profound humility.

We have just read a brief biographical sketch of Imam al-Laqqani. This passage highlights his unique position as a leading scholar of hadith and kalam, his role as a trusted authority in Cairo, and his personal qualities such as dignity, humility, and spiritual attainment. As you read the source, notice how the author weaves together external scholarship and inner spirituality.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once, focusing on the flow of the description. Then read the English translation.
The passage begins with 'فضله' and proceeds in a single continuous description.
2
Identify his scholarly fields
Notice that the passage mentions two specific sciences: hadith and diraya (which includes both transmission and criticism) and kalam (theology). Also note his role as the reference for fatwas.
These fields show his breadth.
3
Reflect on his personal qualities
The passage describes his strong spirit, dignity, aloofness from people, and humility about his noble lineage. Consider why these qualities are mentioned together.
His aloofness is linked to teaching, not arrogance.
4
Consider the spiritual dimension
The text says he combined Sharia and haqiqa, and had miracles. Reflect on how this complements his scholarly image.
5
Summarize his legacy
Based on the passage, write a one-sentence summary of al-Laqqani's character and role.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فضله : كان الإمام اللقاني رحمه الله أحد الأعلام المشار إليهم بسعة الاطلاع في علم الحديث والدراية، والتَّبحر في علم الكلام، وكان إليه المرجع في المشكلات والفتاوى في وقته بالقاهرة، وكان قويَّ النَّفس عظيم الهيبة، يخضع له رجالُ الدَّولة ويقبلون شفاعته، وهو مُنقطع عن التَّردُّد إلى أي أحدٍ من النَّاس، ويصرف وقته في الدرس والإفادة، وكانت قبيلته تنتسب إلى الأشراف، إلا أنه كان لا يُظهر ذلك تواضعاً منه، وقد جمع رحمه الله بين الشريعة والحقيقة، وكانت له كرامات خارقة ومزايا باهرة.
His virtue: Imam al-Laqqani, may God have mercy on him, was one of the great scholars pointed to for vast knowledge in hadith and diraya, and profound expertise in the science of kalam. He was the reference for difficult issues and fatwas in his time in Cairo. He was strong in spirit, great in dignity; men of state submitted to him and accepted his intercession. He refrained from visiting anyone among the people, and spent his time in teaching and giving benefit. His tribe was linked to the nobles, but he would not display that out of humility. He combined, may God have mercy on him, Sharia and spiritual reality. He had extraordinary miracles and dazzling merits.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage describes the virtues and scholarly rank of Imam al-Laqqani. It begins by stating that he was one of the great scholars known for vast knowledge in both the external and internal aspects of hadith (hadith and diraya) and profound expertise in kalam (Islamic theology). He served as the authoritative reference for difficult questions and fatwas in Cairo. The passage then describes his personal qualities: strong spirit, great dignity, such that state officials respected him and accepted his intercession. He was also aloof from frequenting people, dedicating his time to teaching. Despite his noble lineage (to the Prophet's family), he did not openly claim it out of humility. Finally, it notes that he combined both the outward law and inner spiritual truth, and that he had extraordinary miracles and outstanding merits.

Key Terms
علم الحديث
الدراية
علم الكلام
المرجع
الشفاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Laqqani's aloofness from people was due to arrogance or disdain.
Correction: His aloofness was because he devoted his time to teaching and giving benefit, and he did not display his noble lineage out of humility, as stated in the passage.

Checkpoint
What does the passage say about al-Laqqani's relationship with state officials?
A) He was submissive to them
B) They submitted to him and accepted his intercession
C) He avoided them entirely
D) He was appointed by them as a judge

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Laqqani exemplifies a scholar who combined deep expertise in multiple sciences with personal humility and spiritual excellence, making him a trusted authority in both religious and worldly matters.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have status or lineage you are proud of. Al-Laqqani hid his noble descent out of humility. What are you hiding about yourself? Are you willing to downplay your strengths to be humble before Allah?
?
You spend time each day. Al-Laqqani devoted his time solely to teaching and benefiting others. Where does your time go? Will you sacrifice your idle moments to serve others with knowledge?
?
You seek knowledge, but do you have the strong spirit to command respect without seeking fame? Al-Laqqani was mighty yet secluded. Are you willing to be unknown but effective? Resolve one action you will take this week to embody his humility.

The Prophet's Presence at al-Laqqani's Lesson and a Transmitted Benefit
Story of the Prophet witnessing a lesson and a transmitted benefit for newborns.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the spiritual significance of the Prophet's presence at al-Laqqani's lesson and the transmitted benefit of reciting Surat al-Qadr for newborns.

Core Idea
The Prophet's unseen presence affirms the value of sacred knowledge and its blessings.

This passage shares a remarkable story about the Prophet Muhammad attending al-Laqqani's lesson, highlighting the immense honor bestowed upon scholars. It also transmits a special benefit for protecting children through recitation of Surat al-Qadr. These narratives inspire reverence for knowledge and trust in divinely revealed practices.

Guided Path
1
Read the story carefully
Read the anecdote once, noting the characters: al-Shihab al-Bishbishi, Shaykh Hijazi al-Wa'if, and al-Laqqani. Observe the dialogue and the exclamation at the end.
Pay attention to the word 'أبداً' – it may be an exclamation of wonder.
2
Reflect on the spiritual significance
Consider what it means that the Prophet attended al-Laqqani's lesson. This story elevates the status of scholars and the act of teaching. Ask yourself: why would the Prophet physically attend a lesson centuries after his passing?
This relates to the concept of karamah (spiritual favor) for saints.
3
Examine the transmitted benefit
Read the benefit about reciting Surat al-Qadr over a newborn. Note the specific conditions: night of birth, placing hand, reciting the surah. Consider the promised outcome: protection from adultery.
This is a transmitted practice, not an obligation; it reflects reliance on divine protection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حكى الشهاب البشبيشي قال : (ومما اتفق أن الشيخ العلامة حجازي الواعظ وقف يوماً على درسه فقال له الشيخ اللقاني: تذهبون أو تجلسون، فقال له : اصبر ساعة، ثم قال والله يا إبراهيم ما وقفت على درسك إلا وقد رأيتُ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم واقفاً عليه، وهو يسمعك، حتى ذهب ) . أبداً .، وكان رحمه الله كثير الفوائد ومن فوائده المنقولة عنه : أن من قرأ على المولود ليلة ولادته سورة القدر واضعاً يده عليه لم يَزْنِ في عُمره
Al-Shihab al-Bishbishi narrated, saying: Among what happened was that the scholar Shaykh Hijazi al-Wa'if one day stopped at his lesson, and Shaykh al-Laqqani said to him: 'Will you go or will you sit?' He replied: 'Wait an hour.' Then he said: 'By Allah, O Ibrahim, I did not stop at your lesson except that I saw the Messenger of Allah, may God bless him and grant him peace, standing over it, listening to you, until he left.' [Then the narrator exclaims:] 'Forever!' And he (al-Laqqani) had many benefits, and among the benefits transmitted from him is: that whoever recites Surat al-Qadr over a newborn on the night of his birth, placing his hand on him, he will not commit adultery in his lifetime.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage contains two items: a story and a transmitted benefit. The story is from al-Shihab al-Bishbishi, who recounts that the preacher Shaykh Hijazi al-Wa'if once stopped at al-Laqqani's lesson. Al-Laqqani asked him whether he would go or sit. After waiting an hour, Shaykh Hijazi swore by Allah that he had seen the Prophet standing over the lesson, listening to al-Laqqani, until he left. This attests to al-Laqqani's high spiritual rank. The narrator adds 'أبداً' as an exclamation of wonder. The second item is a benefit transmitted from al-Laqqani: that reciting Surat al-Qadr over a newborn on the night of his birth, with the hand placed on the child, will protect him from ever committing adultery.

Key Terms
حكى
درس
رسول الله
فوائد
سورة القدر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the benefit about Surat al-Qadr guarantees protection regardless of other factors, as if it operates automatically.
Correction: The benefit is presented as a transmitted practice (a form of blessing), not a binding promise; its effectiveness depends on divine will and the individual's faith.

Checkpoint
What did Shaykh Hijazi see when he stopped at al-Laqqani's lesson?
A) Angels descending
B) The Prophet listening to al-Laqqani
C) Al-Laqqani performing a miracle
D) A light from heaven

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's attendance at a lesson and the protective benefit of Surat al-Qadr remind us of the spiritual rewards of seeking knowledge and following prophetic practices.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever truly considered that the Prophet ﷺ might be aware of your pursuit of sacred knowledge? How would that awareness change your focus and sincerity in learning today?
?
The benefit of Surat al-Qadr for a newborn promises lifelong protection from a major sin. What sin in your own life are you willing to fight with the same means? Will you commit to reciting this surah over yourself or your children with this intention?

Al-Laqqani's Shafi'i Teachers
List of al-Laqqani's major Shafi'i teachers with their works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key Shafi'i teachers of Imam al-Laqqani and their notable works.

Core Idea
Al-Laqqani's teachers shaped his scholarly legacy.

This passage introduces us to the Shafi'i scholars who taught Imam al-Laqqani. Knowing his teachers helps us appreciate the intellectual lineage behind his famous poem. The passage also directs us to his own biographical work where he recorded all his teachers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation to get an overview of the content.
Pay attention to the names and titles.
2
Identify each teacher and their work
List the three teachers mentioned and note their famous works: al-Bakri, al-Ramli with Nihayat al-Muhtaj, and al-Abbadi with al-Ayat al-Bayyinat.
These works are important references in Shafi'i fiqh and usul.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider how al-Laqqani's teachers contributed to his scholarship and why this lineage matters for his own work, Tuhfat al-Mureed.
Al-Laqqani's own book Nathr al-Ma'athir lists all his teachers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شيوخه: أخذ الإمام اللقاني عن كثير من المشايخ ذكرهم في كتابه: نثر المآثر فيمن أدركت من علماء القرن العاشر . فمن أجل مشايخه : من الشافعية : -1 علامة الإسلام العارف بالله الشيخ الإمام محمد بن أبي الحسن البكري الصديقي. -2 الشيخ الإمام محمد الرَّملي صاحب نهاية المحتاج شرح المنهاج ) . العلامة الشيخ أحمد بن قاسم العبادي، صاحب الآيات البينات على الورقات».
His teachers: Imam al-Laqqani studied under many shaykhs, whom he mentioned in his book Nathr al-Ma'athir fi man Adraktu min Ulama' al-Qarn al-Ashir. Among his most important teachers from the Shafi'is: -1 The sign of Islam, the knower of God, Shaykh Imam Muhammad ibn Abi al-Hasan al-Bakri al-Siddiqi. -2 Shaykh Imam Muhammad al-Ramli, author of Nihayat al-Muhtaj Sharh al-Minhaj. The scholar Shaykh Ahmad ibn Qasim al-Abbadi, author of al-Ayat al-Bayyinat 'ala al-Waraqat.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage lists some of al-Laqqani's teachers, specifically from the Shafi'i school. It begins by noting that he studied under many shaykhs, whom he himself recorded in a book titled 'Nathr al-Ma'athir fi man Adraktu min Ulama' al-Qarn al-Ashir'. Then it mentions three prominent Shafi'i teachers: 1) Muhammad ibn Abi al-Hasan al-Bakri al-Siddiqi, described as 'sign of Islam' and 'knower of God'; 2) Muhammad al-Ramli, famous for his commentary 'Nihayat al-Muhtaj' on al-Minhaj; 3) Ahmad ibn Qasim al-Abbadi, author of 'al-Ayat al-Bayyinat ala al-Waraqat'. These names show the scholarly pedigree of al-Laqqani within the Shafi'i tradition.

?
This lesson shows a student who knew the names and works of his teachers with precise detail. Do you know the names of the scholars you learn from—your current teachers or the authors of books you study? If not, what will you do to change that starting today?

Imam al-Laqqani: Virtues and Miracles
Biographer describes al-Laqqani's learning, authority, miracles, and a transmitted benefit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the extraordinary virtues and miracles of Imam al-Laqqani, including a witnessed visit of the Prophet to his lesson and a transmitted benefit for newborns.

Core Idea
Al-Laqqani's karamat prove that sainthood and deep knowledge go hand in hand.

This passage gives us a glimpse into the life of a towering scholar and saint, Imam al-Laqqani. It describes his vast knowledge, his spiritual authority, and a remarkable miracle that demonstrates his closeness to the Prophet. The passage also ends with a practical blessing for newborns that many parents seek.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to get the overall flow. Notice the three main sections: general virtues, the miracle anecdote, and the transmitted benefit.
The anecdote is introduced by al-Shihab al-Bishbishi.
2
Identify key themes
Identify the qualities of al-Laqqani mentioned: knowledge, authority, humility, detachment, and union of Shari'a and truth. Recognize that the anecdote is a karamah (miracle) of a saint, not a claim of prophethood.
The word 'أبداً' after the anecdote is likely a marginal note, not part of the narrative.
3
Reflect on the transmitted benefit
Consider the practice of reciting Surat al-Qadr over a newborn. Reflect on how the author includes this as a barakah (blessing) transmitted from the saint.
This benefit shows the practical spiritual legacy of al-Laqqani.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كان الإمام اللقاني رحمه الله أحد الأعلام المشار إليهم بسعة الاطلاع في علم الحديث والدراية، والتَّبحر في علم الكلام، وكان إليه المرجع في المشكلات والفتاوى في وقته بالقاهرة، وكان قويَّ النَّفس عظيم الهيبة، يخضع له رجالُ الدَّولة ويقبلون شفاعته، وهو مُنقطع عن التَّردُّد إلى أي أحدٍ من النَّاس، ويصرف وقته في الدرس والإفادة، وكانت قبيلته تنتسب إلى الأشراف، إلا أنه كان لا يُظهر ذلك تواضعاً منه، وقد جمع رحمه الله بين الشريعة والحقيقة، وكانت له كرامات خارقة ومزايا باهرة. حكى الشهاب البشبيشي قال : (ومما اتفق أن الشيخ العلامة حجازي الواعظ وقف يوماً على درسه فقال له الشيخ اللقاني: تذهبون أو تجلسون، فقال له : اصبر ساعة، ثم قال والله يا إبراهيم ما وقفت على درسك إلا وقد رأيتُ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم واقفاً عليه، وهو يسمعك، حتى ذهب ) . أبداً . وكان رحمه الله كثير الفوائد ومن فوائده المنقولة عنه : أن من قرأ على المولود ليلة ولادته سورة القدر واضعاً يده عليه لم يَزْنِ في عُمره
Imam al-Laqqani, may Allah have mercy on him, was one of the eminent scholars pointed to for their extensive knowledge in hadith and its sciences, and for their deep immersion in the science of kalam. He was the reference for difficult problems and fatwas in his time in Cairo. He was strong in spirit, great in dignity; statesmen submitted to him and accepted his intercession. He was detached from frequenting any person, and spent his time in teaching and giving benefit. His tribe traced lineage to the nobility (ashraf), but he did not display that out of humility. He combined sacred law and spiritual truth, and had extraordinary miracles (karamat) and brilliant merits. Al-Shihab al-Bishbishi narrated: 'Among what happened is that the scholar Shaykh Hijazi al-Wa'iz one day stopped at his lesson. Al-Laqqani said to him: Will you go or sit? He said: Wait an hour. Then he said: By Allah, O Ibrahim, I did not stop at your lesson except that I saw the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, standing over it, listening to you, until I left.' Ever. And he, may Allah have mercy on him, had many benefits. Among the transmitted benefits from him: that whoever recites Surat al-Qadr on the night of a newborn's birth, placing his hand on him, that child will not commit adultery in his lifetime.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage is a biographical description of Imam al-Laqqani's virtues and miracles. It begins by highlighting his vast knowledge in hadith and kalam, and his role as the chief authority for resolving difficult issues and issuing fatwas in Cairo. His personality is described as strong and dignified, to the point that state officials would submit to him and seek his intercession. Despite his social influence, he was detached from worldly people and devoted himself to teaching. His lineage was from the ashraf (descendants of the Prophet), but he concealed it in humility. The author emphasizes that he united Shari'a and haqiqa (spiritual reality), and possessed extraordinary karamat (miracles). A specific anecdote is then narrated by al-Shihab al-Bishbishi: The scholar Hijazi al-Wa'iz once came to his lesson, and al-Laqqani asked him to either leave or sit. After waiting, al-Wa'iz swore that he saw the Prophet himself standing over the lesson, listening to al-Laqqani. This miracle underscores his spiritual rank. The passage concludes with a transmitted benefit: reciting Surat al-Qadr over a newborn prevents him from zina (adultery) in his life.

Key Terms
الإمام اللقاني
كرامات
الشهاب البشبيشي
حجازي الواعظ
سورة القدر
الكرامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The anecdote might be misunderstood as a claim that al-Laqqani directly saw the Prophet in wakefulness as a regular occurrence or as a claim of prophethood.
Correction: This was a karamah (miracle) granted to a saint (wali), witnessed by another person. It is not a claim of prophecy nor does it imply that saints can see the Prophet at will.

Checkpoint
Why did Shaykh Hijazi al-Wa'iz say he stopped at al-Laqqani's lesson?
A) He wanted to debate him
B) He saw the Prophet attending the lesson
C) He was forced by the ruler
D) He was looking for a fatwa

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Laqqani combined deep scholarship with spiritual miracles, and his legacy includes a prayer for newborns that reflects his barakah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Imam al-Laqqani hid his noble lineage out of humility. What status, achievement, or lineage do you secretly rely on for your self-worth, and can you truly let go of it for Allah?
?
If you believed that the Prophet ﷺ was physically present at your study session, how would your focus, intention, and preparation change — and why doesn't that knowledge motivate you now, given that Allah sees all?

Al-Laqqani's Shafi'i Teachers: An Introduction
Al-Laqqani's Shafi'i teachers listed and described.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand who al-Laqqani's most eminent Shafi'i teachers were and what contributions they made to Islamic scholarship.

Core Idea
Al-Laqqani learned from four great Shafi'i scholars, each a master in his own right.

In this passage, we are introduced to the scholarly lineage of Imam al-Laqqani. He studied under many teachers, but he highlights four Shafi'i giants who shaped his education. Knowing these names connects us to the chain of Islamic learning and shows the breadth of al-Laqqani's training.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Notice how al-Laqqani introduces his teachers and the descriptors used for each.
2
Identify the four teachers
The passage lists four Shafi'i teachers. List their names and note any distinctive titles or works mentioned.
Each teacher has a short description.
3
Reflect on the chain of learning
Consider why al-Laqqani mentions these specific teachers and what their inclusion says about his own credentials.
This isn't just a list; it's a scholarly pedigree.
4
Test your knowledge
Answer the checkpoint question to ensure you can link each teacher to their famous work.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شيوخه: أخذ الإمام اللقاني عن كثير من المشايخ ذكرهم في كتابه: نثر المآثر فيمن أدركت من علماء القرن العاشر . فمن أجل مشايخه : من الشافعية : -1 علامة الإسلام العارف بالله الشيخ الإمام محمد بن أبي الحسن البكري الصديقي. -۲ الشيخ الإمام محمد الرَّملي صاحب نهاية المحتاج شرح المنهاج . -٣ العلامة الشيخ أحمد بن قاسم العبادي، صاحب الآيات البينات على الورقات».  ترجمة الناظم العلامة الشيخ برهان الدين إبراهيم اللقاني ٤ - العلامة الشيخ علي بن يحيى الملقب نور الدين الزيادي.
His teachers: Imam al-Laqqani studied with many teachers, whom he mentioned in his book 'Nathr al-Ma'athir fiman Adraktu min 'Ulama' al-Qarn al-'Ashir'. Among his eminent teachers: From the Shafi'is: 1. The sign of Islam, the knower of Allah, the shaykh, imam Muhammad ibn Abi al-Hasan al-Bakri al-Siddiqi. 2. The shaykh, imam Muhammad al-Ramli, author of Nihayat al-Muhtaj Sharh al-Minhaj. 3. The scholar, shaykh Ahmad ibn Qasim al-'Abbadi, author of al-Ayat al-Bayyinat 'ala al-Waraqat. 4. The scholar, shaykh 'Ali ibn Yahya, known as Nur al-Din al-Ziyadi.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage introduces the section on al-Laqqani's teachers. It states that he studied with many scholars, whom he catalogued in a separate work. Then it begins listing his 'most eminent' teachers, starting with the Shafi'i scholars. Four Shafi'i teachers are enumerated: (1) Muhammad ibn Abi al-Hasan al-Bakri al-Siddiqi, described as 'sign of Islam' and 'knower of Allah'; (2) Muhammad al-Ramli, famous for his commentary Nihayat al-Muhtaj on al-Minhaj; (3) Ahmad ibn Qasim al-'Abbadi, known for his commentary al-Ayat al-Bayyinat on al-Waraqat; (4) 'Ali ibn Yahya al-Ziyadi. The enumeration is numbered, and the author includes brief descriptions of each teacher's notable works or epithets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Al-Laqqani's Four Hadith Teachers
Lists four hadith teachers of al-Laqqani with numbers 12-15.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the identities and significance of four key hadith teachers of al-Laqqani, revealing the depth of his traditional training.

Core Idea
A scholar's training is rooted in a network of revered teachers.

This passage introduces four of al-Laqqani's hadith teachers, each a notable scholar in his own right. By examining these figures, we gain insight into the scholarly environment of 10th-11th century AH Cairo and the rigorous chain of learning that shaped al-Laqqani's expertise. Let's meet them one by one.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the original Arabic text once. Notice the numbered list and the formal honorifics. Then read the literal translation to grasp the meaning.
Pay attention to the death dates and titles.
2
Meet each teacher
Go through each of the four teachers. Note their names, affiliations, and the specific details mentioned about al-Laqqani's study with them.
3
Identify the most important teacher
The passage states from whom al-Laqqani took the most. Identify this teacher and reflect on why this relationship might be especially significant.
4
Understand the scholarly network
Consider what these teachers represent: different madhhabs (Maliki, Shafi'i), roles (mufti, shaykh of a riwaq), and methods (completing books every three years). This shows the breadth of al-Laqqani's education.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن شيوخه في الحديث: ١٢ - الإمام الهمام أبو النجا سالم بن محمد عز الدين بن محمد ناصر الدين، السنهوري المالكي المصري مفتي المالكية ،ورئيسهم توفي سنة (١٠١٥هـ)، وهو أكثر من أخذ عنه من شيوخه. ١٣ - الشيخ محمد البهنسي، وقد أكثر كذلك في الأخذ عنه، وكان يختم في كلِّ ثلاث سنين كتاباً من أمهات الحديث . ١٤ - الشيخ محمد الوسيمي الشافعي (ت: ١٠٠٦هـ). ١٥ - الشيخ يحيى القرافي المالكي، شيخ رواق ابن معمر بالأزهر.
And from his teachers in hadith: 12. The imam, the hero, Abu al-Naja Salim ibn Muhammad 'Izz al-Din ibn Muhammad Nasir al-Din, al-Sanhuri al-Maliki al-Misri, the mufti of the Malikis and their leader, died in the year (1015 AH). He was the one from whom he [al-Laqqani] took the most among his teachers. 13. Shaykh Muhammad al-Bahnasi, and he also took a lot from him, and he [al-Laqqani] would complete a book from the major hadith collections every three years. 14. Shaykh Muhammad al-Wasimi al-Shafi'i (d. 1006 AH). 15. Shaykh Yahya al-Qarafi al-Maliki, the shaykh of the Riwaq Ibn Ma'mar in al-Azhar.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage lists four hadith teachers. (12) The first is Salim al-Sanhuri, described with many honorifics and noted as the chief Maliki mufti and the teacher from whom al-Laqqani learned the most. (13) Muhammad al-Bahnasi, from whom he also learned extensively; it is mentioned that al-Laqqani would complete a major hadith book every three years under him. (14) Muhammad al-Wasimi al-Shafi'i, with his death year given as 1006 AH. (15) Yahya al-Qarafi al-Maliki, who held the position of shaykh of the Riwaq Ibn Ma'mar at al-Azhar. The passage highlights the depth of al-Laqqani's hadith training.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The phrase 'ختم في كل ثلاث سنين كتاباً' might be interpreted as a general requirement for all students of hadith.
Correction: It specifically describes al-Laqqani's personal habit under the guidance of Shaykh al-Bahnasi, not a universal rule.

Lists three Sufi teachers of al-Laqqani.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will recognize three of al-Laqqani's spiritual guides in the Sufi path and understand the distinction between his academic and spiritual teachers.

Core Idea
Al-Laqqani's spiritual education complemented his scholarly training.

Al-Laqqani's biography is not complete without mentioning his spiritual guides. While his academic teachers are well-documented, this passage introduces three shaykhs who guided him in the Sufi path (tariqa). These names highlight the integrated nature of Islamic learning, where formal scholarship and spiritual purification go hand in hand.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three names
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the three names and their numbers. This is a continuation of the list of teachers, now focusing on the spiritual path.
2
Understand 'في الطريق' (in the path)
The phrase 'في الطريق' refers to the Sufi spiritual path (tariqa). These teachers are not academic scholars but spiritual guides who trained al-Laqqani in inner purification and Sufi practices.
Tariqa is distinct from the academic sciences (fiqh, hadith, etc.) studied earlier.
3
Reflect on the integration of learning
Consider why al-Laqqani sought both academic and spiritual teachers. This reflects the holistic approach in classical Islamic education, where outward knowledge and inward purity are both essential.

Al-Laqani's Teachers: A Scholarly Network Across Disciplines
Biographical list of al-Laqani's teachers by madhhab and discipline.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the breadth of al-Laqani's education through the categorized list of his teachers in jurisprudence, hadith, and spirituality.

Core Idea
Al-Laqani’s teachers spanned fiqh, hadith, and spirituality, grounding him in both law and inner purification.

This passage from the biographical introduction lists the teachers of Ibrahim al-Laqani, the author of Jawharat al-Tawhid. It groups them by legal school (Hanafi, Maliki) and by discipline (hadith, spiritual path). Understanding this network helps us appreciate the scholarly environment that produced his theological masterpiece.

Guided Path
1
Read the list and notice the categories
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Observe how the teachers are grouped: first the Hanafis, then the Malikis, then teachers of hadith, and finally teachers of the spiritual path.
The numbering starts at 4, indicating this is a continuation from a previous page.
2
Identify the two legal schools represented
Determine which madhhabs appear among the fiqh teachers. The passage explicitly mentions 'From the Hanafis' and 'From the Malikis'. Note the names of prominent scholars in each.
No Shafi'i or Hanbali teachers are listed here, though some hadith teachers are identified as Shafi'i.
3
Reflect on the combination of disciplines
Consider why al-Laqani’s education included not only fiqh but also hadith and tasawwuf. This reflects a holistic approach to Islamic learning common among later scholars.
The spiritual teachers (مشايخ الطريق) show his connection to Sufi orders.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical list of the teachers of the author, Burhan al-Din Ibrahim al-Laqani. It begins with the heading 'Biography of the author...' and then lists his teachers, often grouped by legal school (Hanafi, Maliki) or by discipline (hadith, spiritual path). The numbering is inconsistent, starting at 4 (possibly continuing from a previous page). The list includes notable scholars such as Ali ibn Ghanim al-Maqdisi (Hanafi), Umar ibn Nujaym (Hanafi author), and multiple Maliki scholars. The section on hadith teachers highlights two figures: Abu al-Naja al-Sanhuri, the Mufti of the Malikis, and Muhammad al-Bahnasi, who would complete a major hadith book every three years. The final section mentions two spiritual guides: Ahmad al-Bulqini and Ibn al-Turjman, described as a great saint. The list demonstrates the breadth of al-Laqani's education across fiqh, hadith, and tasawwuf.

Al-Laqani's Prominent Students
A list of al-Laqani's students, many of whom became notable scholars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the diversity of scholars who studied under Imam al-Laqani, spanning different legal schools and regions, reflecting his broad influence.

Core Idea
Al-Laqani's students spanned multiple legal schools and regions, proving his widespread impact.

This passage lists seventeen of Imam al-Laqani's most prominent students. As you read through the names, notice the diversity in their backgrounds and affiliations—some were his own family, others came from different lands and followed different legal schools. This list is a testament to his scholarly reach and the high regard in which he was held.

Guided Path
1
Read the complete list
Go through each student entry, noting their names and any titles or descriptions given by al-Laqani.
Pay attention to the opening phrase 'أخذ عن الإمام اللقاني كثير من الأجلاء منهم' which sets the context.
2
Identify the legal schools (madhabs)
Notice which legal school each student belonged to, such as Maliki, Shafi'i, or Hanbali, as indicated by their nisba or description.
Some students are explicitly labeled with their school (e.g., 'المالكي', 'الشافعي', 'الحنبلي').
3
Observe the geographic diversity
Several students are identified by their place of origin or residence, such as Dimashqi (Damascus), Qahiri (Cairo), or Himsi (Hims). Reflect on what this says about al-Laqani's audience.
The list includes scholars from Egypt, Syria, and possibly other regions.
4
Consider the scholarly titles
Note the honorifics used for each student, such as 'الإمام', 'الحافظ', 'الشيخ', 'المحدث', 'الأصولي'. These indicate their areas of expertise and status.
The most elaborate description is given to his son, Abd al-Salam al-Laqani.

The list also includes scholars from various regions (Damascus, Cairo, Hims) and with specializations (judge, adib). This demonstrates the wide influence and reach of al-Laqani's teaching.

١٤ - حسين بن محمود العدوي الزوكاري الصالحي القاضي الشافعي الأديب . 15 - عبد الباقي بن عبد الباقي الحنبلي البعلي الدمشقي، الشهير بابن البدر.
١٦ - عبد القادر بن أحمد الغزي الشافعي، المعروف بابن الغصين.
١٧ - عبد القادر بن مصطفى الصفوري الدمشقي الشافعي .
۱۸ - مصطفى بن أحمد بن منصور أبو الجود بن محب الدين الدمشقي الأديب، وكان الشيخ يخصه بدرس في ألفية الحديث على خلاف عادته من الامتناع عن التخصيص لفرد.
١٩ - عبد الله بن سعيد بن أبي بكر باقشير المكي كبير علماء الحجاز في عصره، توفي سنة (١٠٧٦هـ).
- الشيخ محمد الخراشي المالكي .
۲۱- عمر بن عمر الزهري الدفري الحنفي القاهري.
۲۲- شهاب الدين أحمد الدواخلي.
ولم يكن أحد من علماء عصره أكثر تلامذة منه .
His students: Many eminent persons studied under Imam al-Laqani, among them: 1- His son, Shaykh Abd al-Salam al-Laqani al-Maliki, the imam, investigator, proficient, hadith scholar, usuli, theologian, leader of the Malikis in his time, died in 1078 AH. 2- Shaykh Shams al-Din al-Babili Muhammad ibn Ala al-Din Abu Abdullah al-Shafi'i al-Hafiz. 3- Shaykh Abd al-Baqi ibn Yusuf al-Zarqani. 4- Shaykh Ali ibn Ali Abu al-Diya Nur al-Din al-Shabra Mallisi al-Shafi'i. 5- Yusuf al-Fishayri al-Maliki, died 1061 AH. 6- Yas ibn Zayn al-Din ibn Abi Bakr al-Ulaymi al-Himsi. 7- Husayn al-Namawi. - Husayn al-Khafaji. 9- Uthman ibn Ahmad ibn al-Qadi Taqi al-Din Muhammad, famous as Ibn al-Najjar al-Futuhi al-Hanbali al-Qahiri, died 1064 AH. 10- Ahmad ibn Ahmad al-Ajami al-Shafi'i al-Wafa'i, died 1086 AH. 11- Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Ziryabi al-Dimashqi al-Maliki (1050 AH). 12- Ahmad ibn Yahya ibn Hasan ibn Nasir al-Hamawi, known as Ibn al-Mu'adhdhin, the Shafi'i jurist, Qadiri. 13- Ahmad ibn Yahya ibn Yusuf al-Hanbali al-Karmi (1091 AH). 14- Husayn ibn Mahmud al-Adawi al-Zukari al-Salihi, the Shafi'i judge, the litterateur. 15- Abd al-Baqi ibn Abd al-Baqi al-Hanbali al-Ba'li al-Dimashqi, famous as Ibn al-Badr. 16- Abd al-Qadir ibn Ahmad al-Ghazzi al-Shafi'i, known as Ibn al-Ghusn. 17- Abd al-Qadir ibn Mustafa al-Safuri al-Dimashqi al-Shafi'i. 18- Mustafa ibn Ahmad ibn Mansur Abu al-Jud ibn Muhibb al-Din al-Dimashqi al-Adib, and the Shaykh (al-Laqani) would single him out for a lesson on Alfiyyat al-Hadith, contrary to his habit of refraining from singling out an individual. 19- Abdullah ibn Sa'id ibn Abi Bakr Baqashir al-Makki, the great scholar of the Hijaz in his time, died 1076 AH. - Shaykh Muhammad al-Khurashi al-Maliki. 21- Umar ibn Umar al-Zuhri al-Dafri al-Hanafi al-Qahiri. 22- Shihab al-Din Ahmad al-Dawakhili. And no one among the scholars of his time had more students than him.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is a biographical enumeration of the students of Imam al-Laqani. It begins by stating that many eminent persons studied under him, then lists 22 individuals with brief identifying details. The list includes his son Abd al-Salam, scholars from different madhhabs (Maliki, Shafi'i, Hanbali, Hanafi), and various regions. The author highlights al-Laqani's exceptional teaching by noting that he made an exception for one student (Mustafa ibn Ahmad) by giving him a private lesson, contrary to his usual practice. The passage concludes by asserting that no contemporary scholar had more students, emphasizing his preeminence as a teacher.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The list of students is exhaustive and includes all of al-Laqani's students.
Correction: The passage likely mentions only the most prominent students; other students exist but are not named.

A scholar's teachers and students reveal his intellectual genealogy and legacy.

This passage from the biographical entry on al-Laqqani lists several of his teachers and notes his many students. Let's see who taught al-Laqqani and what his teaching style was like.

The Composition of Jawharat al-Tawhid
Al-Laqqani's composition story for Jawharat al-Tawhid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the circumstances surrounding the composition of Jawharat al-Tawhid and its immediate reception, including the role of al-Laqqani's shaykh and the miraculous production of copies.

Core Idea
A poem of faith written in a single night with miraculous dissemination.

This lesson tells the remarkable story behind the writing of Jawharat al-Tawhid. Al-Laqqani composed this fundamental poem in a single night upon the instruction of his Sufi shaykh. The shaykh's praise and advice, as well as the rapid copying of hundreds of manuscripts, testify to the work's special place in Islamic scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully to understand the sequence of events.
2
Identify the key figures
Note al-Laqqani and his shaykh Ahmad 'Arab al-Sharnubi. Consider the shaykh's role and his advice.
3
Reflect on the miracles
Consider the supernatural aspects: composing in one night, writing 500 copies in a day. What does this tell us about the work?
4
Understand the shaykh's advice
The shaykh advised al-Laqqani to belittle his own right and not to praise the work publicly. Why would he do that? Reflect on humility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
1 - «جوهرة التوحيد: منظومة في علم العقائد ألفها في ليلة واحدة بإشارة شيخه في التربية والتصوف، صاحب المكاشفات وخوارق العادات، الشيخ أحمد عرب الشرنوبي. ثم إنه بعد فراغه منها عرضها على شيخه المذكور فحمده ودعا له ولمن يشتغل بها بمزيد النفع، وأوصاه شيخه المذكور بِغَمط حق نفسه، وأن يترك تزكيتها أمام الناس تورعاً، فما خالفه بعد ذلك أبداً . وحكي أنه كان شرع في إقراء المنظومة المذكورة، فكتب منها في يوم واحد خمسمائة نسخة، ثم أقرأها تلاميذه فيما بعد.
1 - 'Jawharat al-Tawhid': a didactic poem (manzumah) in the science of beliefs (ilm al-aqa'id). He authored it in one night upon the suggestion of his shaykh in spiritual training and Sufism, the possessor of unveilings and extraordinary acts, Shaykh Ahmad 'Arab al-Sharnubi. Then after finishing it he presented it to his aforementioned shaykh, who praised him and prayed for him and for whoever occupies himself with it with increased benefit. And his aforementioned shaykh advised him to belittle his own right and to leave praising it before the people out of scrupulousness, and he never disobeyed him after that. And it was related that he began to teach the aforementioned poem, and he wrote from it in one day five hundred copies, then he taught it to his students afterwards.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage describes the first of al-Laqqani's completed works, Jawharat al-Tawhid, and the circumstances of its composition and dissemination. It states that the work is a didactic poem (manzumah) in the science of beliefs (ilm al-aqa'id). He wrote it in a single night upon the suggestion of his shaykh in spiritual training and Sufism, Shaykh Ahmad 'Arab al-Sharnubi, who was known for mystical unveilings and extraordinary acts. After finishing, he presented it to the shaykh, who praised him, prayed for him and for those who study it. The shaykh also advised him to belittle his own right (i.e., not to claim credit) and to avoid praising the work before people out of scrupulousness (wara'). Al-Laqqani never disobeyed this advice. Additionally, it is related that he began teaching the poem, and in a single day he wrote 500 copies of it, then taught it to his students. This highlights the work's immediate popularity and the author's diligence.

Key Terms
منظومة
علم العقائد
شيخ
تورع
مكاشفات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the shaykh's advice 'to belittle his own right' means he should not claim authorship or that he should give up his rights entirely.
Correction: The phrase actually means to disregard or belittle one's own merit, not to deny authorship. It is a call to humility, not to renounce credit.

Checkpoint

A) 50
B) 100
C) 500
D) 1000

Key Takeaway
The composition of Jawharat al-Tawhid was marked by divine assistance, as seen in its creation in one night and the miraculous copying of 500 manuscripts in a day, while the author maintained humility as advised by his shaykh.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you achieve something praiseworthy, do you tend to credit yourself or recognize Allah's favor? How does al-Laqqani's humility challenge your own attitude toward your accomplishments?
?
The shaykh advised al-Laqqani to 'belittle his own right' and avoid praising his work. Is there an area in your life where you are overly attached to your own efforts or reputation? What would it look like to genuinely let go of that need for recognition?
?
Imagine you were al-Laqqani, having composed a masterpiece in one night. Would you be able to follow the shaykh's advice to stay silent about its merit? What fears or desires would make that difficult for you?

The Passing of Imam al-Laqani
Al-Laqani's death, burial place, and a contemporary elegy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the circumstances of Imam al-Laqani's death, his burial place, and the esteem in which he was held by his contemporaries.

Core Idea
Al-Laqani died returning from Hajj, buried near al-Aqaba, mourned as an irreplaceable imam.

Before delving into a scholar's work, it is valuable to know key events of their life. This lesson covers the death of Imam al-Laqani, the author of Jawharat al-Tawhid. Understanding his passing helps us appreciate the legacy he left behind and the respect he commanded among his peers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Let the biographer's own words convey the facts and emotion.
2
Note the date and place of death
Identify the precise year (1041 AH / 1631 CE) and location (near al-Aqaba on the Egyptian caravan route). This situates al-Laqani in history.
He died while returning from Hajj, a blessed context.
3
Identify the other scholar mentioned
The passage notes that the great hadith scholar Abu al-Abbas al-Maqqari al-Maliki died in the same year. Notice how the biographer connects them.
Al-Maqqari is famous for his work Nafh al-Tib.
4
Read the elegy
Read the poetic elegy by Mustafa al-Dimashqi. Understand that it mourns both scholars as 'two imams after whom time has no replacement.'
The elegy uses poetic imagery: 'the full moon sent tears upon his cheek.'
5
Reflect on the closing prayer
The passage ends with a prayer for mercy upon al-Laqani. Let this inspire gratitude for the scholars who preserved Islamic knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمة الناظم العلامة الشيخ برهان الدين إبراهيم اللقاني
وفاته
توفي رحمه الله وهو في طريق عودته من الحج سنة (١٠٤١هـ) الموافق ١٦٣١م، ودفن بالقرب من العقبة، وكانت بطريق الركب المصري.
وفي هذه السنة توفي الحافظ الكبير أبو العباس المقري المالكي، فقال فيهما مصطفى بن محب الدين الدمشقي يرثيهما :
مضى المَقْرِي إثرَ اللَّقاني لاحقاً
إمامان ما للدهر بعدهما خَلَفْ
فبدر الدجى أجرى على الخد دمعه
فأثر ذاك الدمعُ ما فيه من كَلَفْ
رحمه الله رحمة واسعة، وجعله في عليين.
Biography of the versifier, the learned scholar, Shaykh Burhan al-Din Ibrahim al-Laqani: His death. He died, may Allah have mercy on him, while on his way back from Hajj in the year 1041 AH (1631 CE), and was buried near al-Aqaba, and that was on the route of the Egyptian caravan. And in this year died the great memorizer Abu al-Abbas al-Maqqari al-Maliki, so Mustafa ibn Muhibb al-Din al-Dimashqi said elegizing them both: "Al-Maqqari went following al-Laqani, two imams, after whom time has no replacement. The full moon [reference to one of them?] sent tears upon his cheek, so that tear left a mark in his affection." May Allah have mercy on him with ample mercy and place him in the highest ranks.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note on the death of the author, Ibrahim al-Laqani. It first records the date and circumstances of his death: he died while returning from Hajj in 1041 AH (1631 CE), and was buried near al-Aqaba on the Egyptian caravan route. The passage then notes that in the same year, the great hadith scholar Abu al-Abbas al-Maqqari al-Maliki also died. The biographer quotes an elegy composed by Mustafa ibn Muhibb al-Din al-Dimashqi commemorating both scholars, emphasizing their status as imams whose loss leaves no equal. The passage concludes with a prayer for mercy on al-Laqani.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Imam al-Laqani died while returning from Hajj—the very act of worship that draws one closer to Allah. Are you living your life in a way that, if your final moment came during an act of obedience, you would be content to meet your Lord in that state? What one step can you take today to make your 'return' (from any journey or even daily tasks) one that Allah would be pleased with?

?

If you were to die tomorrow, would your legacy be one that people pray for (as the passage prays for al-Laqani) or one that is forgotten? What change in your daily priorities would make your end more honorable?

Birth and Early Life of Imam al-Bajuri
Al-Bajuri's birth, upbringing, and early education

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the early life of Imam Ibrahim al-Bajuri, including his birth, upbringing, education at al-Azhar, and his most prominent teacher.

Core Idea
Al-Bajuri's early life shows how a student's resolve is tested by hardship, yet leads to scholarly greatness.

This passage introduces us to the commentator of our text, Imam Ibrahim al-Bajuri. Before we dive into his commentary, it is important to know who he was, where he came from, and how he became a leading scholar of al-Azhar. In these lines, we learn about his birth in the village of Bajur, his early Quranic memorization under his father, his journey to al-Azhar, and the historical disruption of the French occupation that briefly interrupted his studies.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Bajuri's biography
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of his early life.
Pay attention to his titles and the mention of his father.
2
Note the key dates and events
Identify the year of his birth (1198 AH/1784 CE), his arrival at al-Azhar (1212 AH), and the French occupation (1213 AH). Understand how these events shaped his education.
The occupation forced him to move to al-Jiza temporarily.
3
Recognize his most prominent teacher
Read about Shaykh Muhammad al-Amir al-Kabir, who granted al-Bajuri an ijaza and influenced his work.
Al-Bajuri's quotations from his teacher show his intellectual lineage.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمة العلامة الإمام إبراهيم الباجوري رحمه الله تعالى
(1)
هو الإمام العلامة المحقق المدقق، بحرُ العلوم، وشيخ المنطوق والمفهوم، شيخ الأزهر؛ برهان الدين إبراهيم بن محمد بن أحمد الباجوري، (ويقال: البيجوري، ولكنه اختار هو نفسه الباجوري) الجيزاوي الشافعي .
ولادته ونشأته:
ولد العلامة الباجوري بمدينة باجور من محافظة المنوفية، سنة ( ١١٩٨هـ / ١٧٨٤م)، والباجوري نسبة إليها، وكان قد نشأ الإمام الباجوري رحمه الله تعالى في حجر والده؛ فحفظ القرآن وجوده عليه .
ثم قدم إلى الأزهر الشريف طلباً للعلم سنة (۱۲۱۲هـ) ، ولكن لما نزل الاحتلال سنة (١٢١٣هـ) سافر إلى الجيزة مدة يسيرة، ليعود إليها عندما رحلت الحملة الفرنسية بعد سنوات ثلاث.
أبرز شيوخه الذين أخذ عنهم :
لعل من أعلى العلماء كعباً شيخه العلامة الشهير الشيخ محمد الأمير الكبير، والذي أجازه بثبته سدّ الأرب»، وقد تجلى ذلك في نقولاته عنه (1)
Biography of the learned scholar, Imam Ibrahim al-Bajuri, may Allah Almighty have mercy on him: (1) He is the Imam, the learned, the verifying, the scrutinizing, a sea of sciences, the teacher of the spoken and the understood, the Shaykh of al-Azhar: Burhan al-Din Ibrahim ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Bajuri (and it is said al-Bayjuri, but he himself chose al-Bajuri), al-Jizawi al-Shafi'i. His birth and upbringing: The scholar al-Bajuri was born in the city of Bajur in the province of al-Minufiyya in the year 1198 AH (1784 CE), and al-Bajuri is a relative attribution to it. Imam al-Bajuri, may Allah have mercy on him, was raised under the care of his father, so he memorized the Quran and recited it well to him. Then he came to the noble al-Azhar seeking knowledge in the year 1212 AH, but when the occupation landed in the year 1213 AH, he traveled to al-Jiza for a short period, to return to it when the French campaign departed after three years. His most prominent teachers from whom he took: Perhaps the highest in status among scholars is his teacher, the famous scholar Shaykh Muhammad al-Amir al-Kabir, who granted him an ijaza with his thabat 'Sadd al-Arab', and that was evident in his quotations from him. (1)
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry on Ibrahim al-Bajuri, the commentator of this work. It begins by praising him with titles such as 'sea of sciences' and 'Shaykh of al-Azhar', gives his full name and preferred nisba (al-Bajuri over al-Bayjuri), and notes his Shafi'i madhhab. Then it describes his birth in Bajur, Minufiyya in 1198 AH/1784 CE, and his upbringing under his father with whom he memorized and perfected Quranic recitation. It then recounts his move to al-Azhar in 1212 AH. When the French occupation of Egypt occurred in 1213 AH, he fled to al-Jiza temporarily, returning after the French left three years later. Finally, it highlights his most prominent teacher, Muhammad al-Amir al-Kabir, who gave him an ijaza (license to teach), and whose influence appears in al-Bajuri's quotations.

الأزهر
محمد الأمير الكبير

The Life and Legacy of Imam Ibrahim al-Bajuri
Biographical account of al-Bajuri's teachers, works, and death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly background, major works, and lasting contributions of Imam Ibrahim al-Bajuri, particularly his gloss 'Tuhfat al-Mureed'.

Core Idea
Imam al-Bajuri's glosses became standard texts in Islamic education.

Imam Ibrahim al-Bajuri was a towering figure in 19th-century Islamic scholarship, known for his precise and elegant glosses on key theological and legal texts. This passage from Tuhfat al-Mureed introduces us to his teachers, his rise to the position of Shaykh al-Azhar, and his prolific authorship. Reading his biography helps us appreciate the authority and depth behind the commentary we are studying.

The list includes many glosses on various subjects.
4
Reflect on his legacy
Consider how his scholarship continued through his students and writings.

المصباح في النكاح. حاشية على التحفة الخيرية على متن الشنشورية في علم الفرائض . أيضاً القول حاشية على فتح القريب المجيب في شرح ألفاظ التقريب، ويسمى المختار في شرح غاية الاختصاره، لابن قاسم الغزي، وهو من أعظم الحواشي المتأخرة في الفقه الشافعي . حاشية على المنهج، ولكن مات قبل أن يتمها . وهي كذلك لم تتم . حاشية على جمع الجوامع في أصول الفقه، الحاشية على المواهب اللدنية على الشمائل المحمدية. — تحفة البيان. فتح الخبير اللطيف شرح نظم الترصيف» في فن التصريف. الدرر الحسان على فتح الرحمن فيما يحصل به الإسلام والإيمان للحافظ الزبيدي . حاشية على متن السلم في المنطق للعلامة الأخضري. حاشية على مختصر السنوسي في المنطق أيضاً . وفاته رحمه الله تعالى: بقي الشيخ على حاله من العلم والتعليم إلى أن ضَعُف فأقام علماء الأزهر نواباً ، عنه في المشيخة يقومون بتسيير الأمور من الفتيا وغيرها، تحت رئاسة الفتيا وغيرها، تحت رئاسة العلامة العروسي الذي صار شيخاً للأزهر بعد ذلك، إلى أن تُوفي الإمام الباجوري رحمه الله سنة (۱۲۷۷هـ)، وصلي عليه في الأزهر المبارك، ليدفن بعد ذلك في تربة القرافة الكبرى.
And among them are the distinguished scholar Sheikh Abdullah al-Sharqawi, the Shaykh of al-Azhar, and Sayyid Dawud al-Qal'awi, and the scholar Sheikh Hasan al-Qawasini, and he (al-Bajuri) received most of his learning from him and from Sheikh Muhammad al-Fadali, whom he accompanied until the year of his death, and he (al-Fadali) explained to him some of his books on creed. And he spent most of his time seeking knowledge and authoring, which he began early, and he continued ascending the degrees of knowledge as his custom until he assumed the position of Shaykh of al-Azhar, and he was the most deserving of it at that time in the month of Ramadan of the year 1263 AH (1847 CE). His works: In spite of his extensive engagement in education and teaching, the Sheikh was prolific in authoring, in many arts and sciences, and his glosses (hawashi) are among the most important and prominent works written in this field, especially the precision in composition and choice of elegant phrases that do not burden their readers, aside from his licenses (ijazat). Among them: his gloss on the text of al-Jawhara, which he named 'Tuhfat al-Mureed 'ala Jawharat al-Tawheed', by its author Burhan al-Din al-Laqani, died 1041 AH. 'A gloss on the text of al-Sanusiyya' by Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yusuf al-Sanusi al-Husayni, died 895 AH. A gloss on 'Tahqiq al-Maqam 'ala Kifayat al-'Awamm' by his teacher al-'Allama al-Fadali, died 1236 AH. A gloss on 'Sharh al-Sa'd li'l-'Aqa'id al-Nasafiyya' by 'Umar ibn Muhammad al-Nasafi, died 537 AH. 'Fath al-Qareeb al-Majeed 'ala Sharh Bidayat al-Mureed fi 'Ilm al-Tawheed' by Sheikh Muhammad al-Sibai'. 'A brief treatise on the science of tawheed'. 'Manh al-Fattah 'ala Daw' al-Misbah fi al-Nikah'. A gloss on 'al-Tuhfa al-Khayriyya 'ala Matn al-Shanshuriya fi 'Ilm al-Fara'id'. Also the saying: A gloss on 'Fath al-Qareeb al-Mujeeb fi Sharh Alfaz al-Taqreeb', called 'al-Mukhtar fi Sharh Ghayat al-Ikhtisar', by Ibn Qasim al-Ghazzi, and it is among the greatest later glosses in Shafi'i jurisprudence. A gloss on 'al-Manhaj', but he died before completing it. And it also was not completed. A gloss on 'Jam' al-Jawami' fi Usul al-Fiqh. A gloss on 'al-Mawahib al-Laduniyya 'ala al-Shama'il al-Muhammadiyya. — 'Tuhfat al-Bashar', which are comments on 'Mawlid al-Mustafa' by Ibn Hajar al-Haytami. Comments on 'Tafsir al-Kashshaf'. — A gloss on 'Qasidat al-Burda' by al-Busiri. A gloss on 'Qasidat Banat Su'ad' by Ka'b ibn Zuhayr, may God be pleased with him. A gloss on the text of 'al-Samarqandiyya' on rhetorical imagery (bayan). 'Fath al-Khabeer al-Lateef Sharh Nazm al-Tarseef' on the art of morphology (tasreef). 'al-Durar al-Hissan 'ala Fath al-Rahman' on what constitutes Islam and faith (iman) by al-Hafiz al-Zubaydi. A gloss on the text of 'al-Sullam' in logic by al-'Allama al-Akhdari. A gloss on 'Mukhtasar al-Sanusi' in logic as well. His death, may God have mercy on him: The Sheikh remained in his state of knowledge and teaching until he became weak, so the scholars of al-Azhar appointed deputies for him in the shaykhdom to manage affairs of fatwa and others under the leadership of the scholar al-'Arusi who later became Shaykh of al-Azhar, until Imam al-Bajuri died, may God have mercy on him, in the year 1277 AH. The funeral prayer was performed for him in the blessed al-Azhar, and he was buried thereafter in the great cemetery of al-Qarafa.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a biography of Imam Ibrahim al-Bajuri. It opens by listing his teachers: Sheikh Abdullah al-Sharqawi, the former Shaykh al-Azhar; Sayyid Dawud al-Qal'awi; and Sheikh Hasan al-Qawasini, from whom al-Bajuri received most of his learning; and Sheikh Muhammad al-Fadali, whom he accompanied until al-Fadali's death and who explained some of his books on creed to al-Bajuri. It then notes that al-Bajuri spent his time seeking knowledge and writing, eventually rising to become Shaykh al-Azhar in 1263 AH. The passage then lists his many works in theology, jurisprudence, logic, and other fields, emphasizing the precision and elegance of his glosses. Among the most notable is his 'Tuhfat al-Mureed' on the Jawharat al-Tawhid. The biography concludes with his death in 1277 AH, his funeral prayer at al-Azhar, and his burial in the Qarafa cemetery.

?

The Works and Death of Imam al-Bajuri
Lists the works and death of Imam al-Bajuri.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the extensive scholarly contributions of Imam Ibrahim al-Bajuri and the circumstances of his death as documented in his biography.

Core Idea
Imam al-Bajuri's commentaries shaped Shafi'i fiqh for generations.

This passage presents the biography of Imam Ibrahim al-Bajuri, a towering figure in the Shafi'i tradition. It lists his numerous works, mostly commentaries (hawashi) that remain influential, and describes his final years as Shaykh al-Azhar. Understanding his life helps us appreciate the chain of scholarship that preserves Islamic knowledge.

He wrote mostly commentaries on standard texts.
3
Reflect on his death

This shows the value placed on scholarly leadership.

Commentary
This passage is a biography of Imam Ibrahim al-Bajuri, a prominent Shafi'i scholar and commentator. It begins by giving his title as 'al-Allama al-Imam'. Then it lists his major works, most of which are commentaries (hawashi) on key texts in fiqh, usul al-fiqh, Arabic sciences, and logic. The list includes his famous commentary on Fath al-Qarib, his incomplete commentary on al-Manhaj, and various works on hadith, tafsir, poetry, and morphology. The biography then describes the circumstances of his death: as he grew weak, scholars of al-Azhar appointed deputies to assist him in his role as shaykh, under the leadership of al-Urusi. He died in 1277 AH, was prayed over in al-Azhar, and buried in the Qarafa cemetery.

Biography of Shaykh Ahmad al-Ujhuri
Brief biographical entry for Shaykh Ahmad al-Ujhuri.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the background and scholarly contributions of Shaykh Ahmad al-Ujhuri, the author of a key commentary on Jawharat al-Tawhid.

Core Idea
A scholar's biography connects us to the living tradition of Islamic learning.

Before delving into the theological arguments of Jawharat al-Tawhid, it is valuable to know the scholar who wrote one of its most important commentaries. Shaykh Ahmad al-Ujhuri was a blind scholar from Egypt who studied and taught at al-Azhar in the 19th century and authored works on logic, creed, and theology. This brief entry from al-Zirikli's biographical dictionary introduces his life and legacy.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage from al-Zirikli once through, then read the English translation. Note the structure: opening honorific, citation, biographical details, and list of works.
The Arabic contains some formatting peculiarities from the source; focus on the content.
2
Identify key biographical details
List the following: his full name, nickname 'al-Darir', his birthplace (Ujhur, Egypt), his residence at al-Azhar, and his death in Cairo. Ask yourself why his blindness is mentioned.
His blindness did not prevent his scholarly achievements.
3
Reflect on his scholarly works
The passage mentions writings on al-Samarqandiyya (logic), al-Sanusiyya (creed), and al-Jawhara (Jawharat al-Tawhid). Consider how these subjects are foundational to Islamic theology and why a scholar would write commentaries on them.
These works show his expertise in both logic and creed.

This passage is a brief biographical entry for Shaykh Ahmad al-Ujhuri, taken from al-Zirikli's biographical dictionary al-A'lam. The passage highlights his scholarly contributions, particularly in logic and kalam.

Key Takeaway
Shaykh Ahmad al-Ujhuri was a blind Azhari scholar whose commentaries on logic, creed, and Jawharat al-Tawhid continue to be studied in the Islamic tradition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have no physical disability like blindness, yet how often do you let small distractions prevent you from studying? If al-Ujhuri could master logic, creed, and theology without sight, what excuses do you have for neglecting your own study of tawhid? Commit to reading one page of his commentary this week.
?
This passage calls al-Ujhuri 'al-Darir' — it is a mark of honor that his blindness did not define him. What weakness do you hide or let define you? How can you turn it into a source of strength in your pursuit of knowledge?
?
Al-Ujhuri 'jāwara' at al-Azhar — he became a neighbor of the mosque, indicating dedication. Are you a neighbor of your local mosque in spirit, or do you merely visit occasionally? What would it take for you to truly 'reside' in the company of knowledge?

Al-Bajuri's Preface and Statement of Purpose
Al-Bajuri praises God, testifies to faith, and explains his reason for writing the commentary.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
Al-Bajuri's preface reveals his humility, reluctance, and scholarly gratitude before embarking on the commentary.

Al-Bajuri begins his commentary with a traditional Islamic preface: praise of God, testimony of faith, and blessings on the Prophet. He then explains what led him to write this gloss on Al-Laqani's poem. His words reveal his humility—he initially hesitated—and his deep appreciation for the poem's merits. This passage sets the stage for the entire commentary.

الحمد لله المنفرد بالإعدام والإيجاد المنزه عن شوائب النقص والإضداد أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله القديم المكلف الأنام بما شاء من الأوامر وأشهد أن سيدنا محمدا عبده ورسوله الصادق الأمين المبلغ عن رب العالمين صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وصحبه جناة المعارف وأزاهير رياض العطور أما بعد فيقول أفقر الورى إلى ربه الراجي محمد الباجوري ذو التقصير إنه لما كان نظم العالم العلامة ذي الفيض الداني الإمام برهان الدين إبراهيم اللقاني الموسوم بجوهرة التوحيد قد نظم فوائد هذا الفن في عقد نصيد وحوى نفائس الدرر ومحاسن الغرر ما يدهش الألباب ويفضي إلى العجب وقد ولع الناس بالدخول في رياض فوائده والاتعاظ بثمار موائده سألني وفد من الإخوان أصلح الله لي ولهم الحال والمآل أن أكتب عليه حاشية تسفر عن مطويات ما فيه من الرموز والأسرار وتكشف عن سدول النقاب والإسرار فلم ينشرح صدري لذلك والله أعلم بما هنالك ثم رفعت زمام العزم نحو رياضه وأوردت الفكر في عبقري حياة وقريحته وذاك بعض شوارج الناظر الهمام مع ما واش النظم ترى [؟] الله عبد الأمر ومع اكتبه عليه ان رات الاعلام وغير ذلك صحافة [؟] الله به السلام فالتقطت منها دررا نفيسة ومحاسن شريفة في سلك التحرير والتصنيف وجعلتها حاشية على هذا المتن الشريف وقد سميتها تحفة المريد على جوهرة التوحيد جعل الله خالصة لوجه الكريم ونفع بها كل من تلقاها بقلب سليم والمرجو ممن أطلع عليها أن ينظر إلي نظر اعتذار ويستر على ما فيها من الهفوات بإسدال الأستار فالصتز [؟] من شيم الكرام وإذاعة الصويرات من داب اللئام والله أسأل وبنبيه الوسل أن يقع في محل القبول إنه خير مأمول وأكرم مسئول وها أنا أشرع في المقصود بعون الملك المعبود.
Praise be to Allah, who is unique in causing non-existence and existence, exalted above any taint of deficiency or opposition. I bear witness that there is no god but Allah, the Eternal, who obligates mankind with whatever commands He wills. And I bear witness that our master Muhammad is His servant and messenger, the truthful and trustworthy, the conveyer from the Lord of the worlds. May Allah bless him and his family and companions, the gatherers of knowledge and the flowers of fragrant gardens. To proceed: The poorest of people to his Lord, the hopeful one, Muhammad al-Bajuri, the one with shortcomings, says: When the composition of the great scholar, the possessor of abundant grace, the Imam Burhan al-Din Ibrahim al-Laqani, known as 'Jawharat al-Tawhid', had organized the benefits of this art in a firm necklace and contained precious pearls and beautiful excellences that amaze minds and lead to wonder, and people became engrossed in entering the gardens of its benefits and benefiting from the fruits of its banquet, a group of brothers—may Allah set right for me and for them their present and future state—asked me to write a gloss upon it that would unveil the contents within it of symbols and secrets and remove the veils of concealment and disclosure. My chest did not open for this, and Allah knows best what lies therein. Then I raised the rein of determination toward its gardens and brought forth thought into its genius life and talent, and that is some of the manifestations of the determined observer along with what... [؟] ...I gathered from them precious pearls and noble beauties in the thread of editing and classification, and I made them a gloss upon this noble text. I have named it 'Tuhfat al-Mureed ala Jawharat al-Tawhid.' May Allah make it purely for His noble face and benefit everyone who receives it with a sound heart. It is hoped from whoever sees it to look upon it with an apologetic eye and to cover its slips with lowered veils, for concealment is among the traits of the noble, while publicizing faults is the habit of the base. I ask Allah, through His Prophet, the means, that it be accepted, for He is the best hoped-for and the most generous sought-after. And now I begin the purpose with the help of the Worshipped King.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is the author's preface (muqaddima) to his commentary, containing praise of Allah, the testimony of faith, and the reason for writing the work. Al-Bajuri begins with the basmala and hamdala, praising Allah for His unique creative power and transcendence above all imperfection. He then testifies to the oneness of Allah and the prophethood of Muhammad, sending blessings upon him and his companions. In the 'amma ba'd' (to proceed), al-Bajuri identifies himself humbly as the poorest of people to Allah, hoping for His mercy. He explains the context: al-Laqani's poem 'Jawharat al-Tawhid' is a masterpiece that has captivated people, and a group of brothers requested al-Bajuri to write a gloss (hashiya) that would unveil its hidden symbols and secrets. Al-Bajuri initially felt reluctant ('lam yansharh sadri') but later resolved to undertake the task, gathering scattered notes and organizing them into this commentary. He named it 'Tuhfat al-Mureed ala Jawharat al-Tawhid' (The Gift of the Seeker upon the Jewel of Monotheism). He asks readers to look upon it with forgiveness and to conceal its shortcomings, emphasizing that covering faults is noble while publicizing them is base. He concludes by seeking acceptance from Allah and announcing his commencement of the intended exposition.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Bajuri wrote the commentary hastily and without hesitation.
Correction: Al-Bajuri explicitly states that he initially felt reluctant (lam yansharh sadri) and only proceeded after careful thought and raising his determination.

Al-Bajuri's preface reveals his humility and scholarly dedication, as he undertook this commentary only after careful reflection and at the request of fellow students.

?
He asks readers to overlook faults and conceal slips. Is there someone whose faults you need to cover this week? How can you actively practice this noble trait, knowing that 'concealment is among the traits of the noble'?
