Life of Imam al-Bayjuri
beginner
6 min
The Broad Category of Imams: Beyond the Four Schools
Commentator explains and expands the phrase 'the rest of the imams'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two interpretations of the phrase 'the rest of the imams' and recognize the many early scholars considered imams beyond the four famous founders.

Core Idea
The 'rest of the imams' includes many scholars, not just the four school founders.

This passage from the commentary on al-Jawhara addresses the phrase 'the rest of the imams' in the poem. The commentator clarifies that while some restrict the term to only the four founders of the major schools, the better interpretation extends it to many other great scholars of early Islam. He then provides a list of notable imams, often with brief descriptions or sayings, emphasizing the breadth of Sunni scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic source and its literal English translation. Pay attention to how the commentator structures his explanation of the phrase.
The passage has a clear logical flow: definition of the phrase, two possible interpretations, preference for one, then a list of scholars.
2
Understand the two interpretations
The commentator mentions two ways to understand the definite article in 'al-a'imma': as referring to a specific covenant (only the four imams) or as indicating perfection (including any true imam). He prefers the second.
This distinction shows the flexibility of classical Arabic and theological language.
3
Identify the listed imams
Under the broader interpretation, the commentator lists several imams: al-Shafi'i, Abu Hanifa, Ahmad, al-Layth, Dawud al-Zahiri, Sufyan al-Thawri, Ishaq ibn Rahwayh, al-Tabari, Sufyan ibn 'Uyayna, and al-Awza'i. Note that Malik is not mentioned here, but presumably included under the four founders.
Each scholar is given a brief title or saying to highlight their stature.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why the commentator took the trouble to expand the list. It teaches us that Sunni Islam honors many early authorities, not just those whose legal schools survive today.
This passage broadens the concept of 'imam' to include experts in hadith, jurisprudence, and piety.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله : (وسَائِرُ الأَئِمَّة ) أي : باقيهم، فـ (أل) في ((الأئمة) للعهد، والمعهود الأئمة الأربعة فقط، والأولى جعلها للكمال لا بقيد عهد الأربعة فقط، فيَدْخُلُ حينئذ على كل من الاحتمالين الإمام الشافعي أبو عبد الله محمد بن إدريس، والإمام أبو حنيفة النعمان بن ثابت والإمام أحمد بن حنبل، ويدخل على الاحتمال الثاني الليث بن سعد، وداود الظاهري، فإنه كان جبلاً في العلم وما نُقل عن إمام الحرمين من أنه لا يُؤخذ بكلام الظاهرية ولا يُعوّل عليه .. فمحمول على طائفة مخصوصة كابن حزم، ويدخل أيضاً : سفيان الثوري، وكان يُسمّى أمير المؤمنين في الحديث. وإسحاق بن راهويه . و محمد بن جرير الطبري.، وسفيان بن عيينة، وكان يقول : (إذا كانت نفس المؤمن محبوسة عن مكانها الجنة بدَيْنِهِ حتى يُقضى فكيف بصاحب الغيبة؟ فإن الدَّيْنَ يُقضى، والغيبة في لا تُقضى) (1) . وعبد الرحمن بن عمر الأوزاعي، وكان يقول : (ليس ساعة من ساعات الدنيا إلا وتعرض على العبد يوم القيامة، فالساعة التي لا يذكر الله فيها تتقطع نفسه عليها حسرات، فكيف إذا مرت ساعة مع ساعة ويوم مع يوم؟)
And His saying: 'the rest of the imams' i.e. the remainder of them. The definite article in 'al-a'imma' is for the specific covenant, and the covenanted are only the four imams. However, it is better to interpret it as for perfection without the restriction of the covenant of only four. Thus, on either interpretation, there enters Imam al-Shafi'i Abu 'Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Idris, Imam Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man ibn Thabit, and Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal. On the second interpretation, there also enters al-Layth ibn Sa'd and Dawud al-Zahiri, for he was a mountain of knowledge. What is transmitted from Imam al-Haramayn that the speech of the Zahiris is not to be taken nor relied upon is borne upon a specific group like Ibn Hazm. There also enters: Sufyan al-Thawri, who was called the Commander of the Faithful in hadith; Ishaq ibn Rahawayh; Muhammad ibn Jarir al-Tabari; Sufyan ibn 'Uyayna, who used to say: 'If the soul of the believer is detained from its place in Paradise by his debt until it is paid, how about the one guilty of backbiting? The debt is paid, but backbiting is not paid.' (1) And 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Amr al-Awza'i, who used to say: 'There is no hour of the hours of this world except that it is presented to the servant on the Day of Resurrection. The hour in which he does not remember Allah will cause his soul to be cut with regrets. How will it be when hour after hour and day after day pass?'
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the phrase 'sā'ir al-a'imma' from the poem. It first distinguishes two possible interpretations of the definite article: the 'specific covenant' which restricts to the four founders of the major schools (Shafi'i, Abu Hanifa, Ahmad, and by implication Malik? Actually Malik is not named here — only the other three are listed). The author then states that it is better to interpret it as indicating perfection, which allows many other imams to enter. On the second interpretation, he lists al-Layth ibn Sa'd, Dawud al-Zahiri (defending him as a mountain of knowledge), and then further scholars: Sufyan al-Thawri, Ishaq ibn Rahawayh, Tabari, Sufyan ibn 'Uyayna, and al-Awza'i. Each is given a brief title or a saying. The passage serves to broaden the category of 'imams' beyond the famous four to include many early authorities, emphasizing the richness of Sunni scholarship.

عبد الرحمن بن عمر الأوزاعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many think that 'imams' in Sunni Islam refers only to the founders of the four surviving law schools (Hanafi, Maliki, Shafi'i, Hanbali).
Correction: The commentator argues that the term should be understood broadly to include many early scholars such as al-Layth ibn Sa'd, Dawud al-Zahiri, Sufyan al-Thawri, and others, who are recognized as imams in knowledge and piety.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the better interpretation of the definite article in 'al-a'imma'?
A) It indicates a specific covenant referring only to the four imams.
B) It indicates perfection and thus includes many imams beyond the four.
C) It indicates all Muslims.
D) It indicates only the early Meccan imams.

Key Takeaway
The Sunni tradition honors many early scholars as imams beyond the four well-known founders, showing the depth and diversity of early Islamic scholarship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How many of the scholars listed in this lesson have you heard of before? Does your limited familiarity with them reflect a neglect of the vast tradition? What will you do to learn more about these imams and their contributions?
?
When you hear the word 'imam', do you instinctively think only of the four school founders? What does this lesson reveal about your own narrowness? Will you strive to honor the broader legacy of Islamic scholarship?
?
Sufyan ibn 'Uyayna warned about the gravity of backbiting. Which scholar mentioned here have you spoken ill of or dismissed without knowledge? How can you seek forgiveness and correct your attitude towards those who preserved the deen?
